APPENDIXD
Recruitment of human subjects
D.1
Initial enrollment
The recruitment of subjects started on 24th of August by distributing a ﬂier around the university campus in
Lyngby. Every interested person received a personal questionnaire with general questions about the applicant,
contact data and some preliminary questions helping to sort out unsuited applicants. One of the main criteria
was their time availability. This was the base for planning the experimental schedule.
The ﬂier claimed that the total amount of hours in the experiment was 30. However, this was changed
before the start of the experiment, because of extra 30 minutes for acclimatization before each session. This
made ﬁnally 35 hours in total. Participants were informed about this change during the introductory interview
one week before the experiment started.
Appendix D.1 presents:
• the ﬂier
• the personal questionnaire
• the contract

STUDENT JOB AVAILABLE 
Take a part in an Indoor Climate experiment in September 
and earn 135 DKK per hour 
 
Participants must be over 18 years old. Good understanding, reading and writing English is required. You will be  
sitting in a climate chamber and fill in questionnaires regarding their perception of the indoor environment.  
During the experiment, you will be exposed to typical office thermal conditions.  
All procedures will be presented during the introduction meeting on 10th September. 
 
As a participant, you will attend 3 hours sessions, each in 9 or 10 separate days, in a period of 3 weeks. The sessions will take place 
at the same time of the day (set down according to participants’ preferences) in the labs of the ICIEE in building 412,  
from 17th September to 7th October.  
In total, you will attend min. 27 hours in the lab, which means you will earn at least 3 645 DKK*! 
*In order to be paid for the experiment, you need to have an account in any Danish bank (known as NemKonto). 
 
If you are interested, please send an email to: indoor.dtu@gmail.com

and Energy, to use my personal physiological data such as skin temperature, height,

use these photographs and personal data for any other purposes other than scientific or 
distribute them to third parties.  
The ICIEE guarantees that the name of the undersigned hereby participant will not be 
mentioned in any publication or report. The name of the undersigned hereby participant 
will be used only for processing his/her payment.

name in any type of written document.

and will be honest in my answers.

D.2 Instructions for participants

D.2
Instructions for participants
Appendix D.2 presents the document with instructions for future participants, that was handed to all applied
candidates attending the introductory interview.
This document introduced the applicants to the general information about the experiment and the pro-
cedure, especially the conditions and the restrictions regarding their participation. Moreover, the types of
questions and answering from the questionnaires were presented and explained to all candidates.
==PAGE:148==
The International Centre for Indoor Environment and Energy  
 
 
              September 2018 
Technical University of Denmark (DTU) 
 
Instruction for future participants 
 
In the following, please find instructions regarding Indoor environment experiment carried out by 
the International Centre for Indoor Environment and Energy, Technical University of Denmark (DTU). 
We kindly ask you to get acquainted with the instructions before the first day of experiment.  
 
General information about the experiment 
The experiment concerns the human CO2 production and its concentration in a typical meeting room 
condition. During the experiment, you will be exposed to the room temperature of 26 °C, while sitting 
in a climate chamber together with other participants and one thermal manikin. There are going to 
be 10 sessions taking place on 10 days for 3 weeks. Every session lasts 3,5 hours – acclimatisation for 
30 minutes before the experiment and 3 hours inside the chamber. 
 
During the experiment, you will assess the indoor environment in provided questionnaires. This is 
described in the later section. Some measurements will be based on your judgments. Therefore, 
please try to be as honest as possible in your judgments. The questionnaires will be filled in the 
beginning of the session and every 60 minutes (i.e. 4 questionnaires in total). 
 
It is extremely important that your olfactory sense is as neutral as possible: 
 
 
You must not change your typical daily diet during the 3 weeks of the experiment (e.g. not 
to go on a diet to reduce your weight); 
 
You must not eat spicy food (chilli, garlic, etc.) on the day prior to the experiment and on the 
experimental day before the session; 
 
You must not use strongly perfumed hygienic products and strong perfumes on the day of 
the experiment;  
 
Please do not drink very strong coffee/tea for one hour prior to the experiment. You should 
be rested on the experimental day; 
 
You must not party or drink alcohol on the night prior to the experiment! 
 
You cannot discuss your votes with other participants so that your judgments can be treated 
objectively. This applies during the experiments as well as after the experiment.  
 
During session, you will be seated around a table together with other participants on a typical office 
chair. Once you sit down and make yourself comfortable, we kindly ask you not to change much your 
body position, especially the distance between your abdomen and the table during the whole 
session. You are not allowed to rotate yourself on the chair or do any other quick movements. During 
the experiment, you cannot chew chewing gum. During those 3 hours in the chamber, you can use 
your smartphone, tablet (no laptop) or any printed material (book, magazine, printed articles, etc.), 
but you have to keep it laid down on the desk!  
 
We kindly ask you not to leave the experimental room during the measurements in the climate 
chamber. Please use the restroom before the experiments! Any leaving of the chamber would greatly 
affect and harm the obtained results. 
 
==PAGE:149==
The International Centre for Indoor Environment and Energy  
 
 
              September 2018 
Technical University of Denmark (DTU) 
 
Please wear on the experimental day some comfortable clothes that you can modify according to 
your thermal preferences, e.g. tank top + shirt + blouse. You will be asked to describe your clothing 
in the pre-questionnaire. It is also important, that you wear same kind of clothing on every session 
(only either thin/thick socks, same shoes, similar kind of top, etc.) 
 
Please note that none except for the experimenters will have access to your judgements, 
performance, and personal details. All recorded data will only be used for scientific analysing 
purposes.  
 
Schedule of the experiment 
There are going to be 10 sessions on 10 measuring days for 3 weeks. Every session lasts 3,5 hours – 
acclimatisation for 30 minutes before the experiment and 3 hours inside the chamber. The sessions 
will take place in building 412 in DTU campus, the same place as the introductory interview. Time of 
all sessions is going to be the same: 
8:30 – 12:00 
The days of the sessions have been scheduled according to your preferences and answers from the 
form you have sent us back. The schedule of the experiment is the following: 
 
Tuesday
Friday 
Saturday
Sunday 
18.9. 
21.9.

25.9.

2.10. 
 
6.10. 
7.10. 
 
We highly appreciate that you are willing to come for the experiment on weekends as well, as this 
made our planning much easier. At the same time, it is necessary that you come on all of those 
scheduled days in the morning. The session time has been extended to 3,5 hours, which means 
that you will get 4 725 DKK. Remember that in order to get the wage you have to attend all 10 
sessions. 
 
Information about the questionnaires 
During the experiment, you will be asked to vote the perception of the thermal environment, 
perceived air quality and your current condition. Your task is to answer how you feel when you are 
in the examined room. The vote will be done using several kinds of scales. The instruction in English 
will be written whenever you vote. Some of the scales that will be used in the experiment are 
exemplified below. 
 
The acceptability scale is a scale that is divided into two parts, the upper and the lower part. At first, 
you have to decide whether the parameter under evaluation is acceptable or unacceptable. If the 
parameter is acceptable you should use the upper part of the scale and whether it is not acceptable 
you should use the lower part of the scale. Then, you should indicate on the scale to which extent 
you evaluate the parameter to be acceptable or unacceptable. You can mark anywhere on the scale 
except placing it in the gap between "Just acceptable" and "Just unacceptable" (Example 1-1). In the 
==PAGE:150==
The International Centre for Indoor Environment and Energy  
 
 
              September 2018 
Technical University of Denmark (DTU) 
 
examples below, the parameter is assessed to be slightly unacceptable (Example 1-2) and very 
acceptable (Example 1-3).

with which you indicate magnitude of your perceptions. You can mark anywhere on the scale. In the 
examples below, the thermal sensation is assessed as more than slightly warm but less than warm 
(Example 2-1).

APPENDIXF
Questionnaires
There were 5 questionnaires in total answered during each session. The schedule for weekdays/weekends,
shown also in Figure 4.22, was following:
• 845/915 - Questionnaire 1
• 900/930 - Questionnaire 2
• 1000/1030 - Questionnaire 3
• 1100/1130 - Questionnaire 4
• 1150/1220 - Questionnaire 5
Questionnaire 1 was ﬁlled in by the subjects after their arrival to the lab premises, asking about their
commuting to the building, their breakfast and the sleep quality from last night.
Questionnaires ﬁlled in in the chamber had three main parts - PAQ, thermal comfort and questions re-
garding sick building syndrome. Questionnaire 2 and 5 additionally included the question regarding subjects’
clothing.
Appendix F presents as an example questionnaires for the last session - Questionnaire 1 from the acclima-
tization part and Questionnaire 5, that included in the end addition general questions about subjects’ comfort
and their feedback about the experiment.

APPENDIXH
Uncertainty of measurements
Appendix H contents the complete results of the measurements uncertainties. The deﬁnition and the method
of deﬁning the uncertainties is described in section 5.1.5.
The data ID uses the same labeling as was used for data collection throughout the whole experiment.
An example of data obtained by INNOVA gas-monitor is "C01-2018-09-18_I2-ch1", where "C01" stands for a
session, followed by date, when the session was performed, "I2" means INNOVA set number 2 and "ch1" stands
for a speciﬁc channel. The speciﬁcation of channels and their placement in the chamber is listed in Table 4.7.
A similar principle was used for the VAISALA transmitters, where "V" simply corresponds to the VAISALA
measuring instrument and "Nxx" is the number of the transmitter. Table H.1 presents the list of the VAISALA
transmitters with their corresponding locations.
Table H.1: VAISALA transmitters’ locations for monitoring CO2 concentration

I.2
Subjects’ feedback on the experiment
In the last questionnaire in the last performed session, the subjects were asked to give a feedback and write
their general comments on the experiment. All comments are presented in this appendix.
The subjects reported the conditions during the experiment as 77 % comfortable, emphasizing mostly not
enough leg room.
Thank you a lot, Mariya and Tereza. You were so good to us all the time. Even there were some troubles in the
end, you ﬁxed it so kindly. All sessions in the experiment passed OK and all conditions were acceptable. I hope you
got what you aimed. Thank you a lot once more.
The experiments were conducted well. Glad to have contributed. A small suggestion would be to provide a bit
more space, like a bigger table. Hope the results turn out ﬁne :)
Everything went smoothly overal, good communication and I did not feel uncomfortable at any point during the
experiment. Thank you for letting me participate! Best of luck :)
Well organized. We could have had more leg space and could have been provided some reading material (maga-
zines, etc.). Friendly organizers. THANK YOU VERY MUCH!
People in charge were nice and friendly. The sitting arrangement was sometimes inconvenient, but not unbearable.
Thank you for organizing the experiments at 9 am on weekends. Good luck!
Overall this was a pleasant experience. Things were professional and ran on schedule. Tereza and Mariya were
inviting and kind throughout the process, and everyone had a good humour about the chamber. Obviously, this was
necessary for the experiment, but the limited leg room was certainly the worst part of the chamber. Best wishes to
Tereza as she begins her writing!
Real windows would be nice. More comfortable chairs, please. Everything else was nice, mostly issues just stiﬀ
furniture and ugly room. Thanks!
==PAGE:187==
APPENDIXJ
Physical measurements’ results
The physical measurements were performed after each session, except DV-57-22-NS-W0. The measurements
were done using the stand placed behind subject 6. This stand was re-located from one measuring point to
another, eight measuring points in total. The locations of the measuring points are shown in Figure J.1.
There were 8 temperature sensors and 6 anemometers attached to the stand. The heights of the sensors are
presented in Figure 4.11. The physical measurements were performed with heated dummies substituting for
the human subjects. Electric bulbs were plugged inside of each dummy. This way enabled to simulate the heat
source as close as possible to the assumption of a real occupant’s heat production.
Appendix J presents the results of room air temperature ti, air speed v and draft rating DR. The results are
graphically presented upwardly in separate heights for each performed physical measurement.
Figure J.1: Arrangement of measuring points for physical measurements with speciﬁed locations of measuring
points
